Wang Delin's Representative, He Zixing, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Suffering in the Snowy Clothes While Fighting the Enemy

National Compatriots Eagerly Awaiting Assistance

General Wang Delin, Commander-in-Chief of the Jilin National Salvation Army, recently sent Councilor He Zixing as a representative to go south through the pass to contact all parties for assistance. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. A reporter from the Japanese-Japanese News Agency interviewed He at the United Liaison Office of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Armies in Shanghai yesterday. According to him, General Wang's army has a total of 70,000 soldiers, stationed in eastern Jilin, along the Middle East and Jidun roads. They currently occupy eleven counties including Dongning, Wangqing, Hunchun, Dunhua, Helong, Shulan, Emu, Antu, Ningan, and Muling (in co-defense with General Li Du). Since the uprising against the enemy, more than 2,500 Japanese soldiers have been killed. The most intense battle was in the south of Jingbo Lake in Ningan County, a few days before Yu (He Zixing referring to himself) set out to enter the pass. In this battle, 700 Japanese soldiers attacked from both sides. Our army lured the enemy deep on one side and defended the mountains on the other. The enemy was surrounded in the plains surrounded by mountains on all sides. More than 300 Japanese soldiers were killed by our soldiers, and countless weapons were captured. The battles at Laoye Ridge in Dunhua County were also very fierce. Our army bravely advanced, engaging in hand-to-hand combat. The Japanese army was exhausted and many committed suicide. Our army has now decided to advance along multiple routes to Jilin, Changchun, and Harbin to eliminate the enemy and the traitors. However, eastern provinces are extremely cold with snow depths of two feet. Our army is still wearing tattered clothes and straw shoes, desperately fighting the enemy. They lack ammunition and supplies. Yu was ordered to disguise himself and enter the pass to report to the compatriots in the pass, hoping to give assistance, then the recovery of lost land will surely be successful.

Russian Goods Begin to Arrive in Shanghai

Large Shipments Must Wait Until Next Spring

White Russians in Shanghai Not Susceptible to Incitement

After the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, Soviet goods will naturally sell well in our country. Some Russian goods have recently arrived. The details are as follows:

Goods: Since the severance of relations, not many Russian goods have been shipped to China. The September 18th and January 28th incidents occurred successively, and China's boycott of Japanese goods began, leading to a large shipment of salmon, with the most arriving in October, totaling 70,000 pieces, which has defeated Japanese seafood products. Recently, Linji Timber Company has ordered a large amount of timber from Russia, which has now been shipped in millions of feet. Kerosene and gasoline have also been shipped successively. Chinese merchants are planning to contact for sales. Russian Suchang coal has better heating power than Japanese coal and is also more affordable. A batch has now been shipped and is already being sold on the market. Match splints are ordered by Chinese merchants from Japan, but many Russian goods have now been shipped. They are sturdy and superior to Japanese goods, and Chinese people are already trying them out. As for head cotton fabrics, only a small number have been shipped. A large number will be shipped in three months.

Shipping: Since the severance of diplomatic relations between the two countries, the Soviet merchant fleet has been reduced to the Shanghai-Vladivostok route and is handled by the East China Railway Society on behalf. Only one ship sails each month, and chartered ships are used for transportation. This year, the Soviet merchant fleet in Shanghai chartered a large number of Chinese ships to transport goods between Kamchatka and Vladivostok. Now that the river is frozen, the chartered ships have been returned to Shanghai. Many ships have arrived in Shanghai in recent days to terminate the contracts, each carrying a batch of goods. After the ice thaws next March, commercial ships will be chartered again for transportation.

Mail Service: Formal regular mail ships between China and Russia have not been operating since the severance of diplomatic relations. Now that the two countries have resumed diplomatic relations and the exchanges are becoming more frequent, the Soviet merchant fleet has decided to resume the regular mail ships between Shanghai and Vladivostok when the northern part of Vladivostok thaws and shipping is smooth. At that time, branches will be established in Hankou, Guangzhou, Qingdao, and Tianjin to operate shipping. It is estimated that the earliest will be in three months.

White Russians: There are six or seven hundred White Russians in Shanghai, living in various places. Recently, there has been a rumor that after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, White Russians will not be able to stay in Shanghai, and there will be danger if they stay. The rumor intends to scare them into leaving Shanghai and going to Manchuria. The source of this rumor is self-evident to those who are discerning. However, most White Russians who have work in Shanghai are unwilling to leave here.

The Commercial Bureau's Twenty Million Loan Case: Chen and Li Accused of Bribery and Abuse of Power

Yesterday's Trial Concluded with Final Arguments

Li Guojie Still Sent to Hospital Under Surveillance

Li Guojie, former General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and Chen Fumu, former Vice Minister of Communications and concurrently Supervisor, due to mortgaging wharves and warehouses to the American China Development Corporation for a loan of twenty million taels of silver, of which seven hundred thousand was paid in advance and taken by Chen Fumu, resulting in bribery and infringement of rights, etc., was reported by Zhu Jiaji, Minister of Communications, who sent Li for investigation by the local court and issued an arrest warrant for Chen Fumu. Now, the court's prosecutor's office has filed a public prosecution against Chen Fumu and Li Guojie.

People Present in Court Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the criminal court held a public trial. The court specially appointed police chief Chen Junfang, police officers Chen Xihui, Zhu Yongqing, etc., to supervise and direct the bailiffs to maintain order in the courtroom. Police were also dispatched to Shanghai Hospital to accompany Li Guojie to the court. After reporting, Criminal Court President Qian Chengjun, along with judges Shen Youqi, Sun Xiaolou, prosecutor Xie Ju, secretary Jiang Meixuan, etc., opened a collegial panel in the first courtroom. Defendant Li Guojie hired lawyers Sha Xunyi, Zhang Yipeng, and Jiang Yiping to defend him. The gallery was already full at this time. Court President Shen Xiqing also had a special seat to observe the proceedings.

Li Sits While Being Interrogated The presiding judge ordered Li Guojie to be brought to court. Li, wearing a black leather coat, was helped to the court by two people, appearing extremely fatigued. The lawyer presented a hospital certificate stating that Li was seriously ill, unable to stand, and requested permission for him to sit during the questioning. The judge granted the request and allowed Li to sit while providing his statement. The judge first asked Li his age, address, and occupation. He answered, "Fifty-two years old, from Hefei, Anhui, residing at 1050 Xiafei Road, formerly the General Manager and Chairman of the China Merchants Bureau. I have never committed a crime before, nor have I joined any party."

The Prosecutor's Indictment At this point, the judge asked the prosecutor to state the main points of the indictment, saying that the defendant Chen Fumu was the Vice Minister of Communications and concurrently Supervisor, and Li Guojie was the General Manager. In July of this year, they mortgaged a large portion of the China Merchants Bureau's property to the American China Development Corporation for a loan. Because Chen Fumu withheld the contract, the China Development Corporation advanced 700,000 taels, which was given to Chen Fumu, resulting in a contract that greatly damaged many rights. The defendants are accused of violating Article 366, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Because they are public officials, they should be punished according to Article 140 of the same law. As for the bribery part, the indictment is based on Article 129. Li Guojie is to be punished according to Articles 74, 70, and 38 of the same law. A public trial is requested. After the prosecutor finished his statement,

The Details of Holding Office The judge then interrogated Li Guojie, asking, "In what year did you become Chairman?" He answered, "From 1924 until now." The judge asked, "When did you become General Manager?" He answered, "I received the order from the ministry on March 26th, and took over the affairs on April 4th." The judge asked, "Who was the minister at that time?" He answered, "Chen Minggui." The judge asked, "Who were the Vice Ministers at that time?" He answered, "Political Vice Minister Chen Fumu, Permanent Vice Minister Yu Feipeng." The judge asked, "What was the connection that led to your appointment?" He answered, "The ministry appointed me as manager because of my connection with the China Merchants Bureau." The judge asked, "Did you know the minister and vice ministers before?" He answered, "No, I didn't know them." The judge asked, "Are you saying that they appointed you as general manager with no prior connection?" He answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "Since there was no connection, were you appointed as general manager to reorganize the China Merchants Bureau?" He answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "Did you come with the determination to reorganize it?" He answered, "I was in the position of a shareholder and hoped to reorganize it."

Four Contracts in Total The judge asked, "What were the reorganization strategies?" He answered, "When I took over, we were at the end of our rope. We couldn't reorganize without a large loan." The judge asked, "Did you proceed with the loan later?" He answered, "Guo Waifeng had this plan last year as a commissioner. If there hadn't been this plan, I wouldn't have dared to take the job." The judge asked, "Is Guo Waifeng's plan the China Development Corporation?" He answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "When did you negotiate with the China Development Corporation?" He answered, "Last July, I joined as Chairman of the Board." The judge asked, "Did you continue to handle it after you became General Manager?" He answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "When were the contracts signed?" He answered, "The initial signing was in early September." The judge asked, "How many contracts were there in total?" He answered, "Four in total: one for construction loan, one for wharf loan, one for ship purchase loan, and one for wharf leasing." The judge asked, "Were they all signed?" He answered, "I signed them according to Supervisor Chen Fumu's orders." The judge asked, "Were all the contracts approved?" He answered, "All of them were approved." The judge asked, "How much was the wharf loan?" He answered, "Ten million." The judge asked, "How much was the construction loan?" He answered, "Ten million." The judge asked, "The ship purchase part was not determined because thirty ships were needed. The price could not be determined in advance. The ships had different sizes and suitability." The judge asked, "How much of the two loans has been paid?" He answered, "The loans have not been paid. The price can only be paid after the bonds are issued. Therefore, we took 700,000 first."

Seven Hundred Thousand Advance The judge asked, "What is this for?" He answered, "Advance payment." The judge asked, "Who brought it?" He answered, "The comprador Shen Litang of the China Development Corporation brought it." The judge asked, "What day was it brought?" He answered, "September 23rd." The judge asked, "Where was it delivered?" He answered, "At my office in the China Merchants Bureau." The judge asked, "Did you issue a receipt?" He answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "Where did the 700,000 go?" He answered, "Given to the supervisor." The judge asked, "What day was it given?" He answered, "Given on the same day." The judge asked, "Directly?" The judge asked, "Directly?" He answered, "The supervisor sent a representative, Huang Jusu, to take it." The judge asked, "What does Huang Jusu do?" He answered, "I don't know. The supervisor called first to have it handed over to the person who came to take it." The judge asked, "When the payment was made on September 23rd, had the supervisor already approved the contract?" He answered, "It had already been approved." The judge asked, "What is the nature of the 700,000 taels?" He answered, "Advance." The judge asked, "Couldn't it be established without paying?" He answered, "The China Merchants Bureau really couldn't do without the loan. Because when it was sent to the supervisor's office for stamping, the development corporation stated that issuing bonds would take time and asked for secrecy temporarily. The supervisor said that it wouldn't be credible without paying cash, so it was used as a deposit."

The Delivery of a Huge Sum The judge asked, "Where did this money go?" He answered, "The supervisor said that this was the whole plan, and he would keep it together for future consolidation." The judge asked, "Why not keep it in the bureau?" He answered, "This was following the orders of my superior." The judge asked, "Are you saying that you don't know where this 700,000 went?" He answered, "We have already handed it over to the supervisor's office for him to keep." The judge asked, "You said that the 20 million was for reorganizing the business. This 700,000 had nothing to do with the reorganization." He answered, "Reorganization cannot be done easily." The judge asked, "After Huang Jusu took the money, did you meet with Chen Fumu?" He answered, "Yes, I did." The judge asked, "Did you ask him?" He answered, "I asked him, and he said that it would be released publicly, but it never came. I later went to Nanjing and Hankou to inspect the current state of the bureau, so I didn't ask anymore." The judge asked, "Didn't you say before that the supervisor had power, and if you didn't give the money, he wouldn't approve it?" He answered, "Because if China doesn't take an advance payment from foreigners, it will all be in vain in the future." The judge asked, "Were most of the 700,000 taels checks?" He answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "Are you saying that the approval came before the money?" He answered, "Yes."

Various Aspects of the Loan The judge asked, "Did Chen Fumu ever release the approved contract?" He answered, "It was released on September 23rd." The judge asked, "Was it released after taking the money?" He answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "Does the construction loan damage the China Merchants Bureau's property?" He answered, "The land has been abandoned for a long time, and there is no money to build. The loss is very large, and it is mortgaged out, and the debt is pressing. Now that it can be built, the debt can also be repaid, and the land price is also rising day by day." The judge asked, "What about the wharf loan?" He answered, "The wharf was originally mortgaged to Jardine Matheson Bank, and it should have been repaid at the end of last year, but there was no money to repay it. If we don't find another way, we will never have money to repay it. Wouldn't it be disposed of by the creditor?" The judge asked, "Does it damage the shipping rights?" He answered, "The China Merchants Bureau only has twenty broken ships. They must be replaced with new ones, but we don't have the power to do it ourselves. We have to borrow the power of others to develop. It is borrowed from the American Dollar Steamship Company, so there is only profit and no loss. As for the supervisor's regulations, we only have to obey the general manager and cannot directly sue the ministry, and are subject to the supervisor's command. Later, I returned from Nanjing, and the China Merchants Bureau had been reorganized. I should hand over the duties, so I reported the previous matters to Minister Zhu."

Prosecutor's Opinion At this point, the lawyer requested to begin the debate. Prosecutor Xie then gave his opinion, saying that the defendants had committed four counts of violating Article 366: 1. handling affairs for others; 2. intending to obtain illegal benefits for oneself or a third party; 3. intending to inflict illegal damage on oneself; and 4. acting in violation of one's duties, causing damage to one's own property. Li Guojie deliberately damaged the China Merchants Bureau, which is very clear. According to the supervisor's regulations, only cleaning up creditor and debtor rights. Furthermore, the China Merchants Bureau is a privately-run state-owned enterprise. According to the private operation there should have been a board meeting. For the state-run Commercial Bureau, the supervising agency is the Ministry of Communications. The illegal elements cannot be obtained with Chen Fumu's order and are not related to the crime. Regarding whether or not there was damage, one cannot determine without an expert assessment. But according to ordinary observation, it is very obvious that the three wharf mortgage contracts contain clauses stating that if the debt is not fulfilled, the creditor has the right to auction it off. Therefore, the defendants are accused of violating the aforementioned article. But being public officials, they are to be punished according to Article 140. Furthermore, the defendant confessed during the investigation that Chen Fumu did not want to give small benefits, so even today when it was sent up it wasn’t issued. I only cared about the big picture, and gave a little to get it issued, which violates Article 129. He asked that a public trial be conducted according to the law.

Lawyer's Defense Defendant's lawyer Zhang stated that since the government sent a commissioner to supervise the China Merchants Bureau, its main body has belonged to the government, and the shareholders' rights have long been stripped away. Therefore, the supervisor and general manager are all appointed by the government and act according to the government's intentions. The supervisor is the representative of the government, so it does not comply with the article on handling affairs for others. As for intending to cause illegal damage, it can be understood by examining the contracts that have been signed and those that have not. The previous interest owed was over one percent, but now it is only nine percent. Regarding the three warehouses, they were originally set up for overseas development, but now they are all dilapidated, so the warehouse receipts are rejected by the banks, and people are unwilling to store goods there. Now, by borrowing the power of others to build new houses, the banks will be effective and can make money. How to repay the ten million taels? They will use the 300,000 taels of rent money and organize a wharf company, with the bureau having half of the profits. In a few years, it can be cleared. This is for the sake of great profit, and it is also for the government to recover state assets. Each share is fifty taels, for a total of forty thousand, which is over two million taels. The various items are less than twenty million, but they mortgaged twenty million. What is the loss? As for the shipping rights, they are exchanging twenty broken ships for thirty new ships, without having to pay money. They are borrowing the joint transportation of Dollar Steamship Company to expand their business. Dollar Steamship Company is only in charge of accounting. What loss of shipping rights is there? This is the way to production. As for the 700,000 bribe, according to various proofs and letters, it is clear that it is a deposit and payment. How can it be done in a personal seat at 3 PM? Advance and subsequent deposits are also common occurrences. Lawyer Sha added that Li Guojie, as far as we can see now, has only benefited the China Merchants Bureau and has not harmed it. The prosecutor also said that without expert evaluation, one cannot determine whether there was indeed damage. So why not investigate and determine the damage before filing a lawsuit? Therefore, it can be considered that it cannot be the main reason for the crime. Moreover, Chen Fumu took the money, according to Article 35 of the Criminal Law, a superior official can take it for safekeeping, so of course there is no crime. Where is the safekeeping actually, that is not related to Li Guojie. Li Guojie was originally a major shareholder, with a strong patriotic heart, and used all his efforts to revive the company, with the intention of completely safeguarding the interests of the country. As for the 700,000 taken by Chen Fumu, according to the interpretation of the Supreme Court, Li Guojie is also a victim. If it were a bribe, why would there be a receipt, and why would it be noted as a deposit, fully proving it was part of the loan? Please declare him innocent. Lawyer Jiang also stated that this case involves a large loan of thirty million and the 700,000 taken by Chen Fumu, which has led to shocking rumors outside. However, a crime must be determined by the suspect's actions, not by speculation. One cannot involve Li Guojie because of Chen Fumu's actions. Attention and comparison should be paid. The China Merchants Bureau already owes 17 million. If it is not managed, the creditors will forcibly execute the auction. Therefore, it is necessary to attract foreign investment to develop the business. Even the Ministry of Finance has borrowed foreign debt to run real businesses. If borrowing foreign debt is a crime, then all the previous finance ministers should be tried for their crimes. Using other people's money to seek profit, compared to the future when the court seals and auctions it off, which is more beneficial? The supervisor is appointed by the government. The general manager obeys the order in everything and believes in the government and believes in the officials' orders. Therefore, Li Guojie is not responsible. Furthermore, Li Guojie was placed under hospital surveillance due to administrative interference after being released on bail by the prosecutor's office, which has not healed his illness. However, Li Guojie was born in Shanghai, lives in Shanghai, and his property is all in the China Merchants Bureau. If there is a risk of escape, he would not go to President Song's residence. Therefore, it can be guaranteed by a lawyer and does not need to be kept under surveillance in the hospital again. The law can sometimes correct the administration.

The Debate Concluded At this point, the judge asked if the parties had any opinions and then announced the conclusion of the debate, setting the verdict for 2 PM on the 27th of this month. Li Guojie was still subject to the previous disposition and sent to Shanghai Hospital for surveillance. The secretary read the record of the proceedings, and the court was adjourned at 4 PM.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seeks to Facilitate Domestic Rice and Wheat

Please Urge Rice Merchants in Fujian and Guangdong Not to Purchase Foreign Rice

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, in light of the abundant autumn harvest nationwide this year, the drastic drop in grain prices, and the continued procurement of foreign rice in areas with circulation difficulties, telegraphed the Fuzhou and Guangzhou chambers of commerce yesterday, asking them to inform rice merchants to prioritize the purchase of domestic rice. Simultaneously, it sent letters to various rice industry groups in the city, such as the Soybean and Rice Trade Association, Rice Shop Association, and Miscellaneous Grains and Oilcake Trade Association, informing them of the procedures for transporting rice out of the province. The telegram is recorded below:

To the Fuzhou and Guangzhou Chambers of Commerce: This year, all rice-producing provinces report bumper harvests. Anhui and Jiangxi rice is allowed to leave the provinces without inspection fees, and the same applies to Jiangsu rice. The government has approved the nationwide circulation of grain, which is now in effect. Please urge rice merchants to cease purchasing foreign rice and prioritize the procurement of domestic rice to prevent a drastic drop in grain prices and the bankruptcy of rural areas. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Respectfully,

Letter: On the 20th of this month, a letter was received from the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation stating that the 5th Executive Committee meeting and the 7th joint meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committee members held on November 21st resolved that, given the drastic drop in grain prices this year and the difficulties faced by farmers and merchants, a request should be submitted to the provincial government to allow the circulation of rice and grain from the province to provide relief. This proposal was the first item discussed at the 551st Provincial Government Committee meeting. It was noted that in years with average harvests, the province's rice and grain production was only sufficient for self-sufficiency, hence the ban on exports in previous years to maintain the people's food supply. This year, however, a bumper autumn harvest is reported nationwide, including in this province, leading to a daily drastic drop in national grain prices. Farmers rely on the autumn harvest for their livelihood after a year of hard work. The current drop in grain prices has had a significant economic impact on farmers in this province. If remedial measures are not taken urgently, the entire province's rural areas are at risk of bankruptcy. In addition to ordering all counties to earnestly manage grain storage according to the previous order and within the specified timeframe, and announcing to all honest gentry and merchants in the province to stockpile food to increase demand and raise grain prices, it is now proposed to temporarily allow the export of food from the province to raise grain prices and alleviate the people's hardship. The resolution awaits public decision on whether or not to approve it. The resolution states that, for the sake of adjusting social finance and rural economic activity, the province's rice and wheat are temporarily permitted to be sold outside the province, but a passport must be obtained from the county government and forwarded to the provincial government for verification. No fees will be charged for the passport. Anyone transporting goods out of the province without a passport will be investigated and punished according to the regulations. The above resolution of the provincial government concerns the food supply of the entire province, and the matter is of great importance. It should be recorded and communicated immediately for implementation.

[Preparations for the Institute of Forensic Medicine Five-Year Plan]

An Interview with Director Lin Jizhi

China's forensic medicine has always been extremely underdeveloped. Whenever difficult cases arise, there is no clear identification to determine the verdict, and foreigners can take advantage of this to accuse China's judiciary of being obscure, infringing on our legal rights. Although negotiations have taken place, nothing has been recovered. The Ministry of Judicial Administration, in view of this, has a plan to set up a forensic research institution. Previously, the 324th Central Political Conference resolved to set up a special institute of forensic medicine. The National Government issued a clear order for the Ministry of Judicial Administration to prepare for this. The ministry then established a medical research institute in Zhenru, west of Shanghai. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency visited Director Lin Ji at the institute in Zhenru yesterday to inquire about the institute's preparation process and future implementation plans. Director Lin provided detailed information, which is recorded as follows.

Preparation Process According to Lin, the Institute of Forensic Medicine, originally named the Institute of Forensic Examination, began preparations in 1929. The following year, land was purchased in Zhenru, Shanghai, to build housing, and various books and machines were purchased in Europe, costing 170,000 yuan. This year, due to the pressure from the Japanese, the site was occupied and temporarily suspended. In April of this year, an order was received from the Ministry to continue preparations. After the Japanese troops withdrew, the site was recovered. After negotiations, there were few losses. However, when inventorying the supplies and equipment, it was found that the necessary instruments and medicines for initial inspections, injury examinations, and disease examinations were not yet in place. Therefore, Secretary Zhang Dachun of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court was requested to assist in the procurement with maximum frugality. As a result, only 26,000 yuan was spent to complete all the currently applicable items and necessary preparations. The preparation office was officially closed at the end of July, and moved into the new building to begin work.

Scope of Responsibilities The institute's scope of responsibilities includes the examination and testing of corpses and physical and documentary evidence related to forensic cases from all provinces and regions, as well as injury compensation, mental state assessment, personal identification, feigned injury and illness, etc. All levels of courts, agencies, and organizations can send cases to the institute. Examinations and tests are conducted according to the latest scientific methods. Individuals can also come to the institute to carry out examinations for themselves and all factual evidence, and the institute will issue identification certificates or proof documents for verification. In addition, the institute will recruit researchers and trainees to train specialized personnel.

Layout and Equipment In addition to the director's office, section chief's office, staff offices, public hall, lecture hall, meeting room, archive room, dormitory, living room, and garage, the institute is equipped with a chemical testing room, physical evidence inspection room, weighing room, puppet room, pathological tissue examination room, bacteriological serology examination room, ultraviolet light analysis room, autopsy room, photography room, first and second consultation rooms, a mental state assessment reception room, waiting room, corpse identification room, corpse preservation cold storage room, animal breeding room, library specimen room, various heavy machinery rooms, refrigeration machines, heating machines, bath machines, and water machines. A morgue is also planned to be built, which is currently being measured and constructed. Next year, it is also planned to build a poison garden to grow poisonous substances. Various large and small instruments and machines in the research institute are ordered from Germany, the United States, and France. Microscopes and various magnifying glasses are all produced by Zeiss. Test reagents, pigments, and chemicals are mostly German and American products. Glassware is partly from Yena and other world factories, and partly from domestic products. Furniture is designed and manufactured by craftsmen. Among the instruments, equipment such as ultraviolet light analysis devices, blood spectrophotometers, microscopic spectrophotometers, micro scales, right-angle illumination measuring instruments, electrical titration devices, microchemical instruments, precision balances, electrically powered mixers, electrically powered precipitators, electrically powered drying ovens, electrically powered water bath devices, electrically powered leaching devices, Whedon incubators, stereoscopic cameras, microphotographic cameras, stereoscopic microscopes, physical evidence reflection machines, evidence photographing devices, firearms and physical evidence, and fingerprint identification equipment are rare and valuable equipment among specialized medical research institutions in China. In addition, there are corpse transport coffins and trucks for transporting patients and goods, which are specially used for transportation. The animal breeding room is used to produce blood identification serum for humans and animals, and parental identification serum. The mental state assessment reception room is a soft-walled room to accommodate mental patients. The cold storage cabinet is equipped with cold air and has 30 corpse platforms to store corpses and prevent them from decaying. These are rare facilities in other medical offices in China. In the future, it is planned to create corpse beautification and long-term preservation services. As for general consultations, autopsies, pathological examinations, physiological examinations, chemical examinations, qualitative and quantitative analysis of animals, bacterial tests, serum cultures, test trials, and other necessary supplies, as well as diagnostic and emergency medicines, various large and small sterilizers, refrigeration machines, carbonic acid gas machines, water filters, hot water machines, distillation water machines, heating furnaces, water towers, the institute has all the necessary large and small water pipes, artesian wells, incinerators, and water platforms. However, the water well was destroyed by Japanese soldiers and a new one has recently been opened and will soon be completed.

Page 11

Cases Accepted Since its opening four months ago, the Chinese institute has handled cases such as the case of Zhang Laosi in Qingpu, whose cause of death from strangulation and hanging was unclear; the case of Xu Zhao in Changshu, whose bones were found drowned and the cause of death was unclear; the case of Jiang Xiaoshu, a four-year-old girl in Shanghai, to determine whether she died from rape; the case transferred from the Nanjing Health Department regarding whether the internal organs of military prisoner Lang Mengzhong died from illness or poisoning; the case transferred from the Peking Medical College to determine whether the remaining bones burned in the murder case at Xingfenglou in a certain county were human bones, male or female bones, new or old bones, bones of the elderly or young, and whether they were burned before or after death; the case of Zhang Xiaofa in Nantong to determine whether the mooncakes were poisonous; the case of Li Yongquan in Shandong regarding the examination of the internal organs and bones of his two young daughters for poison; the case transferred from the Academia Sinica regarding the bones and blood-stained clothing unearthed from a monastery in Yixing; and the case of Chen Amao in Chongming County, whose cause of death was unknown. These were all sensational and unsolvable cases that have been resolved. Other cases related to poison testing, drug testing, addiction testing, injury testing, blood testing, fingerprint testing, etc., have been sent to the institute for examination and identification by courts or agencies from as far as Hebei and Hunan, and as near as Zhejiang and Shanghai.

Financial Allocation The Institute of Forensic Medicine's regular budget for 1932 is 59,760 yuan, or 4,980 yuan per month. Currently, it has been ordered to reduce the amount by 10%, resulting in 4,482 yuan (details of the allocation are omitted).

Additional Purchases The equipment for forensic examination and research should include the equipment of all departments of medical schools, hospitals, pharmaceutical schools, or chemical colleges. The more complete the equipment and books, the more convenient the identification will be, not only increasing the speed but also facilitating the search for evidence. Due to budget limitations during the preparation period, only the essential equipment was purchased, so it is necessary to continue to add to it in the future. The most important items are: (1) an X-ray machine; (2) reference books related to forensic medicine and chemical examination, and subscriptions to various forensic journals from various countries, as well as self-made charts, plant specimens, and models; (3) other chemical and investigative instruments and equipment. Future Plans The institute has also formulated methods for future plans, which will be carried out in stages. Plans for next year (1933) include: (a) training forensic medicine and forensic chemistry personnel; (b) expanding the poison garden; (c) building more dormitories; (d) expanding the photography room and book storage room. Plans for 1934 include: (a) public research; (b) establishing an investigation department; (c) training criminal police; (d) establishing a branch of the Institute of Forensic Medicine in Peiping. Plans for 1935 include: (a) adding a mental assessment room, reception room, research room, miscellaneous items room, and scattered buildings; (b) establishing more branches; (c) sending personnel abroad to study forensic facilities in various countries. Plans for 1936 include: (a) establishing a school; (b) expanding the institute's organization; (c) building more school buildings. Plans for 1937 include: (a) establishing a mental hospital; (b) planning a smoking cessation center for opium addicts.

Tariff Law Under Study

Whether Tax Rates Will Be Included Is Undecided

According to the Central News Agency, Zhou Dian, the deputy chairman of the National Tariff Commission, told reporters yesterday that the drafting of the tariff law has been under constant consideration and research by the customs authorities for the past two years. Recently, Shanghai business circles have petitioned the central government to expedite the formulation and promulgation. The Ministry of Finance is now actively working to implement it as soon as possible. As for the content, in addition to the administrative law governing tariffs, whether the tax rates will be included is something I do not yet know. The U.S. tariff law includes all types of tax rates, while the Japanese tariff law is formulated separately. It would be easier for our country to follow the latter, but if we follow the former, then all types of tax rates must also be included, resulting in many clauses and a more complicated draft. As for whether the part of the law related to tax rates will be re-examined by the Tariff Commission, it is currently unknown. The Sino-Russian commercial treaty and the Sino-Japanese commercial treaty, which expires in March next year, have not yet been ordered by the Ministry to be drafted. According to past practice, such treaties are drafted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and other relevant agencies, and then the articles on commercial tax rates are submitted to this committee for research. It is expected that the Sino-Russian and other commercial treaties will also be submitted to this committee for research after they are drafted.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seeks Opinions on Partnership Withdrawal

No Regulations in Civil Code Regarding Partnership Withdrawal Procedures

Letter Sent to Various Trades to Express Opinions Fully

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that due to the lack of proper withdrawal procedures for partnerships in the city's partnership stores, various disputes often arise after partners withdraw mid-term. Therefore, the Chamber has specifically sent a letter to various trade associations to solicit opinions and practices on partnership withdrawal. The original letter states: "It has been observed that in our country, most stores are organized as partnerships. Moreover, money lenders place great emphasis on the credit and assets of the partners. Therefore, the withdrawal of a partner, especially one with significant assets and credit, often affects the interests of creditors and raises questions of liability after withdrawal. Creditors often argue that without procedures such as endorsement, amendment, and public notice, the withdrawal cannot be asserted against third parties. While the Civil Code addresses the terms of withdrawal and the issue of liability after withdrawal (limited to debts incurred by the partnership before the withdrawal), it does not specify whether public notice is a necessary procedure. The intention of the relevant clauses is that liability for debts incurred by the partnership before the withdrawal remains, even after public notice. The issue arises with debts incurred by the partnership after the withdrawal; whether such debts can be considered valid if the withdrawal was not publicly announced. According to the principle that if there is no legal provision, custom should be followed, the crucial question is whether endorsement, amendment, and public notice can be considered customs in this city. The establishment of a custom requires both subjective and objective elements: (1) it must be believed by the general public, and (2) there must be continuous and widespread facts. Although some trades practice endorsement, amendment, and registration, the general public does not consider them necessary, so they cannot yet be regarded as customs. Furthermore, partnership stores rely on the credit and assets of the partners, similar to unlimited liability companies. Shareholders of unlimited liability companies must apply to the authorities for registration when withdrawing shares. Therefore, unless proper procedures are established and uniformly applied by all trades for partners withdrawing from partnerships, various disputes will inevitably arise in the future, leading to conflicting views. Consequently, the seventh executive committee meeting resolved to: (1) solicit information from various trades about the customs of partnership withdrawal, and (2) determine proper procedures to be followed for mid-term withdrawals to prevent future disputes. A corresponding record is hereby enclosed for your review and research. Please express your opinions fully and return them to the Chamber by January 15, 1933, for consideration."

Shanghai North District Fire Brigade Urges Allocation of Funds

The Shanghai Zhabei Fire Brigade Joint Association and various fire brigades have been suffering greatly since the restoration, due to the difficulty in claiming the original monthly funds from the Public Security Bureau each time. The accumulated wages of firefighters, the expenses for repairing vehicles and equipment damaged in the war, are all urgently needed. The various brigades are already struggling to cope. Yesterday, they convened a meeting of all fire brigades to discuss the situation, feeling that it was increasingly unbearable. The brigades then elected representatives, who, along with a formal petition, went to the Municipal Government to appeal. Secretary-General Wang received them and stated that the temporary fire-fighting expenses for each war zone had indeed been approved, but due to the emptiness of the municipal treasury, the funds had not been allocated. He acknowledged that the difficulties presented by the brigades were genuine and promised to inform the Finance Bureau to allocate the funds within this year and to ensure that the monthly regular fees would be allocated within a week, specifying a date for future collections to avoid further difficulties. The brigade representatives were satisfied and returned to their respective brigades.

The Sino-German Organizations Joint Association, a collective of Sino-German cultural and academic organizations in Shanghai, aims to promote Sino-German culture, foster friendship, and jointly engage in academic research and knowledge exchange. Yun Case Appeal Judgment

Sentence of Three Months Imprisonment

Yun Huifang, a member of the "Blood Soul" group, was charged because her comrade Cai Yaozu threw a bomb into the Yongchang Coal Company, owned by the traitorous merchant Wu, who sold Japanese coal on Xinza Road on the morning of July 28, causing minor injuries to the employee Yu Ruiliang’s thigh. She was suspected of being an accomplice. The Public Concession Police Department brought Yun before the Second Special District Court. After investigation, the First Special District Court sentenced Yun to three months imprisonment. Yun immediately declared her dissatisfaction and, through her lawyer, filed an appeal with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, listing various reasons for a reversal. The Second Branch of the High Court held two hearings to gather witness testimony and concluded its research. Yesterday, at 2:00 PM, the verdict was announced. Yun Huifang, who had already been released on bail, did not appear despite being summoned. None of her three defense lawyers were present. Only Li Zhishan, the lawyer for the Public Works Department, and the Chinese and Western detectives handling the case arrived on time. Subsequently, Criminal Tribunal President Yu Hua, along with judges Guo and Cai, and the prosecutor and clerk, entered the courtroom and called for the appellant Yun Huifang, but there was no response. President Yu then announced the main text of the judgment: the original judgment regarding the main sentence and commutation was overturned. Yun Huifang was sentenced to three months of imprisonment for harming someone using methods sufficient to cause death or serious injury. The number of days detained before the judgment was finalized will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of two days of detention for one day of imprisonment. The other parts of the original verdict were dismissed.

Zhao Jinji Thermos Bottles Are Not Domestic Goods

First Rejected for Membership by the Trade Association

Then Expelled from the Shanghai West National Goods Exhibition

A Guowen News Agency report states that Zhao Jinyuan, from Pudong, operates the Zhao Jinji Thermos Bottle Factory at 424 Oujiali, Oujia Road, Hongkou. He produces various sizes of Jinshi brand thermos bottles and has achieved considerable success. However, his factory lacks the equipment and workers to manufacture thermos bottles. All of his products are purchased from the Jinlong Thermos Bottle Factory, established by a Japanese man named Guantian. After Zhao Jinji relabels them, they are sold by the Jinhua store on Laobeimen Street to various ports, both domestically and internationally, achieving widespread sales and significant profits. Recently, Zhao Jinji placed advertisements in major newspapers, offering low-priced gifts and claiming to be a member of the Mechanical Industry Association and the National Goods Factory Joint Association. The National Goods Factory has issued a statement denying this and, after investigating, found him to be highly suspicious, publicly denouncing him and urging everyone to reject him. However, Zhao Jinyuan has shown no remorse, fully demonstrating his ability to deceive the Chinese people. Recently, when the Shanghai West National Goods Mobile Exhibition opened, Zhao Jinji also attempted to participate, hoping to deceive society. However, the organizers of the exhibition discovered this and expelled him yesterday, as a warning to shameless merchants. It is reported that the Thermos Bottle Trade Association is paying close attention to this matter and has rejected his application for membership.

Continued Request for Loans to Rebuild Homes for Refugees in Zhabei

Since the war, the farms and residences in Zhabei have been largely destroyed by fire. The refugees from fourteen settlements, including Baziqiao, Gujiazhai, Xiyaozhai, Baojiazhai, Caijiazhai, Xijiawan, Liujiaqiao, Zhuangjiajiao, Donghengbinzhai, Xiajiazhai, Tanjiamuqiao Wangjiazhai, Tanjialong, and Yujiazhai, have already received assistance from the War Zone Relief Association. Each household is entitled to a loan of one hundred and fifty yuan for rebuilding their homes. The first installment of fifty yuan per household has already been distributed in full. Other refugee households from various settlements were scattered and could not be registered immediately. Upon hearing this news, numerous refugees from various settlements in Zhabei have flocked to the Zhabei Refugee Joint Association to request assistance. It is estimated that there are thirty-four households in Gujiawan, ten households in Qujiaqiao, eighteen households in Tanjiatou, ten households in Gejiazui, nine households in Xi Baziqiao, three households in Yusan Dian, eighteen households in Xujiaqiao, thirty-five households in Haijiaqiao, thirty households in Xi Hengbinzhai, and eleven households in Zhao Jiazhai. Other affected settlements are still being registered, totaling approximately more than three hundred households. Adjournment of the Liu Chongwu Case Trial

In recent months, Liu Chongwu and others have followed in the footsteps of Yun Huifang, using drastic measures to deal with unscrupulous merchants in the city, resulting in the tragedy of shooting and injuring people. The police authorities believe that this greatly hinders public security and have ordered all police stations to conduct strict investigations. Liu and others were subsequently arrested one after another. After repeated investigations, in addition to releasing those who were not involved, the Public Works Department filed a lawsuit against Liu and seven others in the First Special District Court. The trial was originally scheduled to be heard by Judge Qian Wenji yesterday afternoon. The lawyers defending the defendants, including Chen Tingrui, appeared in court one after another. However, due to certain reasons, the court adjourned the trial for the sake of prudence. At the same time, it notified the police station to ensure that the prisoners were brought to court. Therefore, it seems unlikely that this case will be heard this year.

Another Accomplice of the Kidnappers in the Liu Nianchun Case Captured

Liu Nianchun, the owner of Dingkang Gold Shop on Tianjin Road, was kidnapped in the autumn of the year before last. After the case was solved, several kidnappers were arrested and executed. Recently, Yang Asi, a native of Tongzhou who was the lookout for the case, was arrested by the Chief Inspectorate of the General Police Station. After repeated investigations by Chinese detectives Lu Liankui and Liu Shaokui, Yang confessed that his accomplice, Zhuang Longhai, was hiding in the Yangshupu area. At 7:30 PM the day before yesterday, Lu and Liu led detectives Xie Futang and detectives from the west to rush to the address to arrest him. Zhuang was arrested near the intersection of Pingliang Road and Shenglu Road. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi questioned him. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated that since Zhuang was Yang's accomplice and the investigation was still ongoing, he requested an adjournment so that the case could be tried together with Yang's. Judge Wu briefly questioned Zhuang and ordered him to be detained for further questioning.

Widow's Remarriage Leads to Trouble with Hoodlums

Husband Injured by Beatings

Zhou Xiaomei, a local woman, is 29 years old and lives in a bungalow on Pingliang Road. Her husband, Zhou Jinfu, died of illness in October, leaving her with nothing. Xiaomei found it difficult to make ends meet and, being young, could not remain celibate. She planned to remarry someone reliable to ensure her future livelihood. A fellow villager, Zhou Yuangou, only 24 years old, was unmarried and worked in a yarn factory. His monthly salary of about twenty or thirty yuan could support a household. Through an introduction, he and Xiaomei agreed to marry, and they began living together early this month. However, tragedy struck when Zhou Jinfu's relative, Xu, a local tanner who associated with hoodlums, learned of the marriage. Citizens Petition the Municipal Government Against Telephone Rate Hikes

The Nanjing Road Business Association and the First District Citizens' Association, in opposition to the concession's telephone rate increases, sent two representatives, Ji Jiannan and Shi Zongtang, to the Municipal Government with a petition yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. He will order Zheng Baocheng, the chief of the bureau who originally handled the case, to come to the government tomorrow (today) to discuss it further and then report it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for processing, so that it can be resolved as soon as possible. The representatives were satisfied and left. Yesterday, the association sent two representatives, Ji Jiannan and Shi Zongtang, to the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities to request a prompt review so that the dispute could be resolved as soon as possible. If it is not resolved soon, it will inevitably develop into a major incident. Death from 打花會

A Warning to Gamblers

Sun Long氏, a local young woman, is 17 years old and lives in a certain building behind the Golden Grand Theatre on 敏體尼蔭路 in the French Concession. Her husband is a detective, nicknamed "Little Kai." The night before last, she lost ten yuan gambling at 打花會. Her husband found out and complained. Afterwards, she felt extremely depressed and conceived the idea of suicide. She secretly took a large dose of 生烟. Someone noticed and immediately took her to Renji Hospital for treatment, but she died at 9:30 PM last night. The hospital reported the death to the 嵩山路 Police Station, and detective 王立羞成 went to investigate. The body was taken to 同仁輔元堂 and will be examined by the court this morning.

Arrest for Manufacturing Fake Silver Coins

Zhou Afu, a native of 羅店, was secretly manufacturing fake silver coins made of lead in a small room at No. 144 杜神父路 in the French Concession for use in the city, disrupting the financial order. A detective from the French Police Station learned of this and went to arrest him on the 10th of this month. Eight fake silver coins, five powder models, dry batteries, and other equipment were seized and taken to the police station. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution according to Article 22 of the Criminal Law, and the case was under investigation. The police investigation has now been concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge 熊代 continued the trial in the criminal court. Police lawyer 費席珍 explained the police investigation situation during the adjournment. According to the detective's report, the process of arresting the defendant was explained. Zhou Afu confessed that he was secretly manufacturing coins for profit. The court ordered the defendant to demonstrate the manufacturing process in court, and the fake coins fit the models without error. Then, the court appointed lawyer 朱殿卿 to defend the defendant. The court declared the debate closed and waited for the scheduled sentencing. The defendant was returned to custody.

News from Various Hometown Associations

The Sichuan Hometown Associations in Shanghai, Tianjin, Beijing, and Wuhan had previously established a joint office of Sichuan Hometown Associations abroad in Beijing. Yesterday, representatives of the Shanghai Association 鍾行素, Tianjin representatives 王藻華, Wuhan representatives 殷仲橋, and Nanjing representatives 朱國定 carried a petition to the Three People's Principles Association: (1) The Central Government should enforce the Seventeen-Year Governance Program in Sichuan and issue an order to end the war within a specified time limit, and those who violate it will be investigated and punished. (6) Establish a Sichuan Army Legacy Association. (7) Convene a Provincial People's Congress. The General Secretary of the Congress, Ye Chucang, met with them. 鍾行素 handed over the petition and explained the reasons. The representatives also added detailed explanations. Ye replied that the entire petition was to the point and was not different from the Central Government's current plan to govern Sichuan. The Wang case will also be handled according to law. However, to stop the Sichuan war by force, it is necessary to send troops to Sichuan. Some people may mistakenly believe that this is an extension of the civil war. Zhong continued to say that the Central Government is to punish the perpetrators and is not comparable to the melee of equal warlords. If the Sichuan turmoil is not stopped decisively this time, the war will be prolonged, and the Sichuan people will either die in the rain of bullets or be killed by whippings. Ye replied that the seven points in the petition and the supplementary statements were all appropriate and will be submitted to the Congress for combined discussion. After the resolution, a written reply will be sent at a later date. The representatives were satisfied and left.

Central Bank Inspection Report

146th Time

The Central Bank's 146th Inspection Report on Issuance Preparation stated that the Committee is responsible for inspecting the gold reserve for redemption of Central Bank notes, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations. On December 20, 1932, Supervisor Yu Qiaqing conducted the 146th inspection at the Issuance Bureau of the Bank. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of silver notes issued is 36,966,987 silver dollars, including 33,244,351 silver notes and 3,722,636 subsidiary coins. The total amount of gold reserve for redemption is 36,966,987 silver dollars, including 30,037,987 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 26,359,539 yuan stored in the Bank's issuing treasury, 1,826,295 yuan stored in branches in various ports, and 1,852,153 yuan deposited with peers. The collateral is prepared to be converted into 6,929,000 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of cash notes issued is 425,000 yuan. The total amount of cash note reserve is 425,000 yuan. This reserve includes 170,000 US dollars deposited with peers in the city, equivalent to 425,000 yuan at a fixed price of 4.0. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's regulations on gold reserve for redemption, the cash reserve is 60% and the collateral reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the collateral is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This is a special report. December 20, 1932, Central Bank Supervisory Committee.

Occupation and Society

(1) Discussion on the question raised by Mr. Weng

丨Original letter see the 19th of this month丨

Zhu Yingjun's letter: The reporter replied to Mr. Weng's letter, saying: "If you can't be the principal, the whole family can go to work. As long as you can endure hardship, you will never starve to death! If you think it is shameful to work, then your own thoughts are falling, and we have no way to do it." The words are very right, but under the current entire social and economic situation, taking Shanghai alone, I don't know how many original workers have lost their jobs? Weng Jun is a weak scholar, and his whole family has never worked before. What kind of work can they do? Which factory is willing to hire them? I have seen many people who have graduated from universities or have been officials. They are very willing to work with their wives, and they have taken off their long gowns and suits and put on workers' clothes, but either the factories do not add people, or they do not want novices. As for saying? "As long as you can endure hardship, you will never starve to death." I want to ask again: "The old people in Shaanxi and Gansu... which one is not more than twelve points more able to endure hardship than us, but why did so many people starve to death? Let me say another sentence: If a certain university graduate wants to work as an extremely low-level worker in your newspaper, with a solid guarantee, can your newspaper accommodate him? Please answer the above questions.

Reply: We think that the questions raised in the letter are very meaningful. However, in our last reply to Mr. Weng, we once said this: "This is actually a whole social problem, and it is difficult to provide individual relief. Therefore, your letter asks us to give a complete answer. We don't have a way, but it is a long story, and the result is still unable to solve your immediate needs." Therefore, we never knew that this was a "whole society" problem, we never knew the difficulty of finding a job in the current society, we never knew the old people in Shaanxi and Gansu, they were "able to endure hardship", but the result was still "starving to death". The words we answered to Mr. Weng were to hope that Mr. Weng would, before the whole social problem was solved, use his own ability to find a way to treat his feet when they hurt and his head when it hurt. Naturally, we are not satisfied with this method, but we cannot let people sit and wait, and not solve the personal problems until the whole social problem is solved. If you must ask us to set a fundamental solution, we can answer you that there are already many scholars who are studying how to reform the social system, right? As for your question: If "a certain university graduate wants to work as an extremely low-level worker in this newspaper, with a solid guarantee, can this newspaper accommodate him?" I also want to ask you first, in the current society, are there only one unemployed person like a certain university student? If there is only one person, we can answer "accommodate" without hesitation. If there is more than one person, there are hundreds of thousands or even tens of thousands of people, then our answer is undoubtedly "no", because using a chariot to help the crowd, although it is said to be a happy thing, but what if the "crowd" cannot "help"?

(2) Discussion on the question raised by Mr. Bao Zhizheng

丨Original letter see the 17th of this month丨

Fu Kebai's letter: (1) Because of the darkness of this entire political system, we can only unite everyone and refuse to pay "black fees". If the Public Security Bureau takes further measures to impose oppression, then everyone must recognize that we cannot be safe unless we overthrow this dark organization! Naturally, the fundamental way is to transform this social system to be useless. (2) This kind of occupation is fundamentally a way, but in the current situation of China's rural economic bankruptcy, if we want to find a new way out, Bao Jun can only use the spirit of self-awareness to make universal propaganda to the 90 people in the same industry and even the vast number of oppressed people, and turn this miserable life into a lively revolutionary path. .

(3) Discussion on the question raised by Mr. Wu Sijing

丨Original letter see the 17th of this month丨

(1) Jiang Cun Song's letter: The reasons why a few people can have food to eat without relying on their knowledge and ability are: (1) liking flattery, (2) loving to save face, (3) taking care of private feelings, (4) not having a long-term vision, (5) lacking the ability to identify; on the part of the employed, (1) being good at flattering, (2) being good at adapting, (3) climbing to the powerful, (4) not having integrity. The reason why most honest and frank people with considerable skills to make a living have food to eat is that they do not have the above reasons, and there are more general reasons, that is, there are more monks than porridge, there are fewer people who are willing to start a business, and there are more people who want to eat ready-made food.

(2) Fu Kebai's letter: Because society is in the hands of these few people, most people cannot get food to eat despite having the skills to make a living. Wu Jun and even the unemployed in general do have the right to demand that society provide them with work, but if you don't transform this society, who will listen to your demands! Friends, society is dead, and it always needs human power to push it around!

Announcement: Due to the problem of disease in this column, we must be diagnosed by a doctor before we can determine the treatment method. There are many gaps in answering questions by correspondence, and we are deeply afraid of delaying the patient and violating the initial intention. From today onwards, we hope that readers will stop sending letters of this kind. As for the letters that have been received, we will still carefully consider and answer them separately. In addition, readers are requested to attach sufficient return postage for future letters, otherwise we will not reply.

Jiangsu Education Expense Management Office Sends Personnel to Urge Borrowing

Half-month fee notice issued

But still short of 100,000 in cash

More than 30 representatives from various schools attending the Temporary Full-Power Representative Assembly of the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Teachers and Staff Association, because the Jiangsu Finance Department owes 3 million yuan in provincial education expenses (more than 1.9 million yuan in owed expenses from counties before May 19, more than 700,000 yuan owed after the division in May, and 365,000 yuan owed in provincial subsidies in the 19th and 20th years, totaling the above numbers), and the Education Expense Management Office recently telegraphed to prepay half of the new arrears (365,000) to meet emergency needs, but has not yet made a firm statement, specially met with Yang Zishen, section chief of the Management Office, and took a car from Nanjing to Zhenjiang on the morning of the 19th. After gathering at Zhenjiang Middle School, they went to the Finance Department in the afternoon, met with the Director of Finance, and discussed until late, but did not get a penny. Director Yang went to the Finance Department again on the 20th, but did not get anything important. The Management Office originally planned to raise funds in three ways: (1) urging the Finance Department to pay arrears, (2) urging loans from various counties, and (3) borrowing from banks. They hoped that the Finance Department would at least pay more than 100,000 yuan from the new arrears of 365,000 yuan, so as to raise cash for two and a half months for provincial schools. Now that they have suffered this blow, they do not know how to make things right. It is heard that the Management Office has issued notices of expenses for the second half of August to provincial secondary schools and social education institutions, and expenses for the second half of October to teachers' schools and experimental primary schools (teachers' schools and experimental primary schools have always been advanced, so they are issued until October). The date for the payment notice is filled in as December 25. The half-month expenses of each school and institution are calculated to be 124,500 yuan. Currently, the Management Office only has more than 20,000 yuan in stock. Therefore, although the notice has been issued, there are still five days until the 25th, and there is still a shortage of 100,000 yuan in cash. During these few days, special efforts must be made to raise funds. It is heard that Section Chief Hua Beihe of the Management Office is scheduled to go to Wujin and Wujiang counties on the 21st to urge loans (Wujin previously lent 50,000 yuan, but has not borrowed a penny so far, Wujiang lent 60,000 yuan, and has remitted 15,000 yuan. It is hoped that these two places will be handled as previously agreed), in order to raise 100,000 yuan by the 25th, so that each school can receive the expenses on time.

Chen Xifang, the second section chief of the Su Education Department, and Xiang Jutan, the third section chief, have already reported the previous report on their trip to Haimen from Tongru to inspect education. After inspecting Haimen, the two section chiefs went to Qidong on the 15th. The county is divided into three school districts. They sometimes inquired about the truth about the extracurricular activities of elementary school children, and then gave detailed guidance to teachers on how to improve them. They set up folk education centers and villages, and personally went to people's homes to ask about the actual situation of social education on the ground. They gave very detailed instructions to the staff of the folk education centers. They have been in Qidong for three days. It is heard that they are satisfied with the education in the county in the following aspects: (1) Expenses can be paid on a monthly basis, (2) The bureau formulates the points of attention for the improvement of schools and social education institutions at all levels every academic year, and most schools and institutions can earnestly follow them. (3) The Education Bureau can indeed follow the... promulgation of the three-year implementation plan for promoting folk schools and set up public schools, and each folk agricultural education center can also follow the rules to supervise the progress of folk schools in each district. There are also several points that are considered to need immediate improvement: 1. Each school is too early in the morning; 2. The homework and arithmetic always need to be corrected; there are many omissions; 3. The single-level education is mostly illegal. Jinan University Heavily Penalized for Leaving the Field Before the End of the Game

Captain Suspended for One Season

Membership Will Be Revoked for a Second Offense

Result of Donghua Match Established

Resolutions of the Western League Executive Committee

The Western League Football Association Executive Committee held a meeting on Tuesday evening and resolved: On the 18th, in the preliminary round of the International League, Scotland vs. Jewish, a Jewish player arbitrarily kicked someone. From the date of the meeting, the player's eligibility for matches is revoked for one month. Regarding the dispute during the Donghua vs. Jinan University match on the 17th, where Jinan University left the field before the end of the game, four resolutions were made as follows:

1. The baseball field is revoked as the home field. The Chinese baseball field is revoked as Jinan University's home field until the end of this 1932-1933 season.

2. Unconditional expulsion for a second offense. The entire Jinan University team is given a serious warning. If a serious incident occurs again among the players, Jinan University will unconditionally have its membership in the Western League Football Association revoked.

3. Captain suspended for one season. The captain of the Jinan University team during the match against Donghua is suspended from participating in matches until the end of the 1932-1933 season.

4. The result of the match is recognized as valid. The result of the Donghua vs. Jinan University match is recognized as valid according to the referee's report.

The committee further stated that, at any time, players who commit any serious violations of regulations, whether in inter-port team selections or other representative teams, will not be included for discussion.

Basketball Friendly, Zhijiang Loses to Shanghai University, Result 61 to 34

Zhijiang Will Play Jiaotong Tonight

The Hangzhou Zhijiang University basketball team played a friendly match against the Shanghai University team yesterday in Yangshupu. One is known for its strength in West Lake, and the other is famous on the sea. As a result, Shanghai University relied on its excellent coordination and accurate shooting to gain the upper hand. Zhijiang, on the other hand, was unfamiliar with the venue. As a result, they lost to Shanghai University by a score of 34 to 61. Although their skills are not as good as Shanghai University's, their movements are clean and their fighting power is strong. Their coordination is also impressive and not weaker than other teams in Shanghai. Tonight at 7:00 PM, Zhijiang will go to Xujiahui Jiaotong University for a match. Jiaotong University's basketball has improved a lot recently. It is unknown who will win this battle. The situation of yesterday's battle is as follows:

▲Shanghai University Is Smooth Sailing. Referee Lu Zhongen blows the whistle to start the game. Zhijiang takes the lead, and the momentum is like a broken bamboo. Shanghai University's Qian Jingyong opens the record, and Zhijiang's Wang Pusheng and Zhang Guowei score six points in a row, taking a 6-2 lead. But from then on, Shanghai University finds ways to score from all directions, and the score increases repeatedly. In addition, the beauty of the short passes wins the cheers of the audience. In a short time, Shanghai University wins with a score of 18 to 6. Zhijiang works hard to score, and Jin Shuxian adds two points. Shanghai University's Jing Jingyong and Feng Nianhua run around the court, making them difficult to catch, and score repeatedly, soaring to a score of 37 to 15 to win the first half.

▲Zhijiang Tries to Catch Up. After the break, Shanghai University fights tirelessly and scores repeatedly. Zhijiang also makes a strong counterattack and does not show weakness. From the score of 56 to 17, Shanghai University's Qian and Feng forwards and defender Sun Shiqing leave the court, and Shi Jiaju, Zou Qiyu, and Yuan Wu fill in, and the combat power is slightly reduced. Zhijiang's entire army is launched, and Wang Pusheng and Zhang Guowei repeatedly make achievements. Chen Yaosheng and Fan Guoxiong respond in the back, and the lineup is consolidated, with no weaknesses. At this point, Shanghai University can only resist and cannot attack. As a result of the battle, Shanghai University scored 61 points, and Zhijiang scored 34 points. The results are as follows:

The Philippines Also Strives for the Far Eastern Games in Two Years

|Early Opening of the Carnival|

(Manila Dispatch) Japan is preparing for the Far Eastern Games in two years. The Philippine Sports Association, in order to wash away the shame of finishing fourth in the last Far Eastern Games and to prepare for the tenth Far Eastern Games to be held in Manila in two years, has now decided to open the 1933 Carnival early on February 4 (the official session is in mid-February). The reason for the early opening is that the Philippine Association requires the expansion of various sports programs in the Carnival to awaken the attention of the people of the entire Philippine Islands to sports. In addition to various sacrificial programs and election programs in the conference, the sports programs should be all-inclusive, including track and field, swimming, football, basketball, volleyball, netball, baseball, boxing, wrestling, bicycle racing, etc. Netball will be expanded, and famous netball players from various parts of Southeast Asia will be invited to participate in the Philippines to promote the past achievements of Philippine players in netball competitions. The netball competition of the Carnival has begun to reserve seats, and tickets are divided into three types: ten pesos, three pesos, and one peso (note: peso is the name of the Philippine currency).

Pudong Retains the Shanghai Middle School Cross-Country Championship

Second Place: Guanghua... Third Place: Jinan... Fourth Place: Shanghai High

▲····················▲

Individual Champion: Zhan Yiji from Guanghua

Time: 19 minutes, 11.52 seconds

Pudong Middle School, relying on the evenness of its talent, yesterday retained the Shanghai Middle School Sports Federation cross-country championship, scoring a total of 45 points. The event was held at Zhenru yesterday at 3 PM, with athletes from eight schools participating. Pudong finished in 5th, 6th, 7th, 8th, 9th, and 10th place, taking the lead and winning the championship. The individual first place was won by Zhan Yiji from Guanghua High School Affiliated, with a time of 19 minutes, 11.52 seconds.

Sixty-Eight Competitors Start

A total of sixty-eight athletes participated in the competition, lined up west of the Jinan University office building, next to the faculty dormitory on a stone road. At the time, the north wind was blowing strongly, and the cold air was biting. The athletes rubbed their fists and prepared themselves, full of vigor. Upon hearing the starter Hao Chunde's command, they sprinted north, leaving Jinan University through the back gate and entering the desolate fields, stumbling along and fighting against the north wind, striving for the championship.

Zhan Yiji Wins First Place

From north to east, from east to south, then turning west, they entered the main road from Shanghai to Zhenru, entered the Jinan University gate, and stopped after about a hundred yards, totaling five kilometers. The first to arrive was Zhan Yiji from Guanghua, taking 19 minutes, 11.52 seconds. After crossing the finish line, he collapsed on the ground and could not get up, a testament to his courageous effort. Fifty yards later, Hua Chongli from Guanghua followed. After that, they arrived successively, with a total of sixty-six people finishing the race.

Pudong Wins the Championship Again

Pudong Middle School won the championship in the previous competition and retained the victory this year. Because the school is located in the countryside, the training is diligent, so it is full of talent and has outstanding achievements. Its top six students came in sequence, reaching the finish line one after another, which can be said to be quite skillful. It scored 45 points with 5th, 6th, 7th, 8th, 9th, and 10th place. The second place in total score was Guanghua, with 92 points.

Award Ceremony After the Race

After the competition, everyone gathered in the Jinan University auditorium. After the recorders calculated the total scores of each school, Ms. Zheng presented the awards. The champion team, Pudong Middle School, received a championship flag and cheered three times before dismissing. Jinan University provided refreshments to treat the athletes and staff of each school.
